  <script type="text/javascript">
    (function() {
        var contextPath = '/jira';
        var eventBuffer = [];

        function printDeprecatedMsg() {
            if (console && console.warn) {
                console.warn('DEPRECATED JS - contextPath global variable has been deprecated since 7.4.0. Use `wrm/context-path` module instead.');
            }
        }

        function sendEvent(analytics, postfix) {
            analytics.send({
                name: 'js.globals.contextPath.' + postfix
            });
        }

        function sendDeprecatedEvent(postfix) {
            try {
                var analytics = require('jira/analytics');
                if (eventBuffer.length) {
                    eventBuffer.forEach(function(value) {
                        sendEvent(analytics, value);
                    });
                    eventBuffer = [];
                }

                if (postfix) {
                    sendEvent(analytics, postfix);
                }
            } catch(ex) {
                eventBuffer.push(postfix);
                setTimeout(sendDeprecatedEvent, 1000);
            }
        }

        Object.defineProperty(window, 'contextPath', {
            get: function() {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('get');
                return contextPath;
            },
            set: function(value) {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('set');
                contextPath = value;
            }
        });
    })();

</script>

              <div id="descriptionmodule" class="module toggle-wrap">
               <div id="descriptionmodule_heading" class="mod-header">
                <ul class="ops"></ul>
                <h2 class="toggle-title">Description</h2>
               </div>
               <div class="mod-content">
                <div id="description-val" class="field-ignore-highlight"> 
                 <div class="user-content-block"> 
                  <p>We need an objective way to measure the performance of Lucene, both indexing and querying, on a known corpus. This issue is intended to collect comments and patches implementing a suite of such benchmarking tests.</p> 
                  <p>Regarding the corpus: one of the widely used and freely available corpora is the original Reuters collection, available from <a href="http://www-2.cs.cmu.edu/afs/cs.cmu.edu/project/theo-20/www/data/news20.tar.gz" class="external-link" rel="nofollow">http://www-2.cs.cmu.edu/afs/cs.cmu.edu/project/theo-20/www/data/news20.tar.gz</a> or <a href="http://people.csail.mit.edu/u/j/jrennie/public_html/20Newsgroups/20news-18828.tar.gz" class="external-link" rel="nofollow">http://people.csail.mit.edu/u/j/jrennie/public_html/20Newsgroups/20news-18828.tar.gz</a>. I propose to use this corpus as a base for benchmarks. The benchmarking suite could automatically retrieve it from known locations, and cache it locally.</p> 
                 </div> 
                </div> 
               </div>
              </div>

\u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12436934_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'22\\/Sep\\/06 17:31\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2006-09-22T17:31:13+0000\'\u003e22\\/Sep\\/06 17:31\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e  \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eA few notes on benchmarks:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eFirst, it is important to realize that no benchmark will ever fully-capture all aspects of lucene performance, particularly since so many real-world data distributions are so varied.  That said, they are useful tools, especially if they are componentized to measure various aspects of lucene performance (the narrower the goal of the benchmark it, the better a benchmark can be created).\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIt is rather unrealistic to expect to standardize hardware \\/ os ... better to compare before\\/after numbers on a single configuration, rather than comparing the numbers among configurations.  The test process \u003cem\u003eis\u003c\\/em\u003e important, but anything crucial should be built into the test (like the number of iterations; taking the average, etc).  Concerning the specifics of this: Requiring reboots is onerous and not an important criterion (at least for unix systems-\u003cdel\u003eI\'m not sufficiently familiar with windows to comment).  Better to stipulate a relatively quiscient machine.  Or perhaps not\u003c\\/del\u003e-it might be useful to see how the machine load affects lucene performance.  Also, the arithmetic mean is a terrible way of combining results due to its emphasis on outliers.  Better is the average over minimum times of small sets of runs.  \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eOf course, any scheme has its problems.  In general, the most important thing when using benchmarks is being aware of the limitations of the benchmark and methodology used.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"klaasm\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12436934_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=klaasm\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"klaasm\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Mike Klaas\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12436934_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'22\\/Sep\\/06 17:31\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2006-09-22T17:31:13+0000\'\u003e22\\/Sep\\/06 17:31\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    A few notes on benchmarks: \\n\\n First, it is important to realize that no benchmark will ever fully-capture all aspects of lucene performance, particularly since so many real-world data distributions are so varied.  That said, they are useful tools, especially if they are componentized to measure various aspects of lucene performance (the narrower the goal of the benchmark it, the better a benchmark can be created). \\n\\n It is rather unrealistic to expect to standardize hardware \\/ os ... better to compare before\\/after numbers on a single configuration, rather than comparing the numbers among configurations.  The test process  is  important, but anything crucial should be built into the test (like the number of iterations; taking the average, etc).  Concerning the specifics of this: Requiring reboots is onerous and not an important criterion (at least for unix systems- I\'m not sufficiently familiar with windows to comment).  Better to stipulate a relatively quiscient machine.  Or perhaps not -it might be useful to see how the machine load affects lucene performance.  Also, the arithmetic mean is a terrible way of combining results due to its emphasis on outliers.  Better is the average over minimum times of small sets of runs.   \\n\\n Of course, any scheme has its problems.  In general, the most important thing when using benchmarks is being aware of the limitations of the benchmark and methodology used.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n You know, for the visual folks   \\n\\n Anyway, my other idea is that benchmarking Lucene can be performed on two levels: one is the user level, where the entire operation counts (such as indexing, searching etc). Another aspect is measurement of atomic parts  within  the big operation so that you know how much of the whole thing each subpart takes. I wrote an interesting piece of code once that allows measuring times for named operation (per-thread) in a recursive way. Looks something like this: \\n\\n perfLogger.start(\\\"indexing\\\"); \\ntry { \\n  .. code (with recursion etc)  ... \\n  perfLogger.start(\\\"subpart\\\"); \\n  try {  \\n\\n   } finally  \\n{\\n     perfLogger.stop();\\n  }\\n } finally { \\n  perfLogger.stop(); \\n} \\n\\n in the output you get something like this: \\n\\n indexing: 5 seconds; \\n   -&gt;subpart: : 2 seconds; \\n   -&gt; ... \\n\\n Of course everything comes at a price and the above logging costs some CPU cycles (my implementation stored a nesting stack in ThreadLocals). \\n\\n One can always put that code in \'if\' clauses attached to final variables and enable logging only for benchmarking targets (the compiler will get rid of logging statements then). \\n\\n If folks are interested I can dig out that performance logger and maybe adopt it to what Grant comes up with.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12436980_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'22\\/Sep\\/06 19:19\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2006-09-22T19:19:06+0000\'\u003e22\\/Sep\\/06 19:19\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    Few things that would be nice to have in this performance package\\/framework -  \\n\\n () indexing only overall time. \\n() indexing only time changes as the index grows (might be the case that indexing performance starts to misbehave from a certain size or so). \\n() search single user while indexing \\n() search only single user \\n() search only concurrent users \\n() short queries \\n() long queries \\n() wild card queries \\n() range queries \\n() queries with rare words \\n() queries with common words \\n() tokenization\\/analysis only (above indexing measurements include tokenization, but it would be important to be able to \\\"prove\\\" to oneself that tokenization\\/analysis time is not hurt by  a recent change). \\n\\n () parametric control over: \\n() () location of test input data. \\n() () location of output index. \\n() () location of output log\\/results. \\n() ()  total collection size (total number of bytes\\/characters read from collection) \\n() () document (average) size (bytes\\/chars) - test can break input data and recompose it into documents of desired size. \\n() () \\\"implicit iteration size\\\" - merge-factor, max-buffered-docs \\n() () \\\"explicit iteration size\\\" - how often the perf test calls \\n() () long queries text \\n() () short queries text \\n() () which parts of the test framework capabilities to run \\n() () number of users \\/ threads. \\n() () queries pace - how many queries are fired in, say, a minute. \\n\\n Additional points: \\n() Would help if all test run parameters are maintained in a properties (or xml config) file, so one can easily modify the test input\\/output without having to recompile the code. \\n() Output to allow easy creation of graphs or so - perhaps best would be to have an result object, so others can easily extend with additional output formats. \\n() index size as part of output. \\n() number of index files as part of output   \\n() indexing input module that can loop over the input collection. This allows to test indexing of a collection larger than the actual input collection being used.  \\n             \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv id=\\\"comment-12440990\\\" class=\\\"issue-data-block activity-comment twixi-block  expanded\\\"\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap verbose actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Collapse comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-expanded\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eHide\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-links\\\"\u003e\\n                \u003ca href=\\\"\\/jira\\/browse\\/LUCENE-675?focusedCommentId=12440990&page=com.atlassian.jira.plugin.system.issuetabpanels:comment-tabpanel#comment-12440990\\\"\\n                   title=\\\"Right click and copy link for a permanent link to this comment.\\\" class=\\\"activitymodule-link issue-comment-action\\\"\u003e\\n                    \u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-link\\\"\u003ePermalink\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n                                            \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details\\\"\u003e        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"gsingers\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12440990_verbose\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=gsingers\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"gsingers\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Grant Ingersoll\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - The interesting thing about this approach, is it is easy to adapt to be more or less exhaustive (i.e. how many of the parameters does one wish to have the system alter as it runs)  Thus, you can have it change the merge factors, max buffered docs, number of documents indexed, number of different queries run, etc.  The tradeoff, of course, is the length of time it takes to run these.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eSo my question to those interested, is what is a good baseline running time for testing in a standard way?  My initial thought is to have something that takes between 15-30 minutes to run, but I am not sure on this.  Another approach would be to have three \\\"baselines\\\":  1. quick validation (5 minutes to run...) 2. standard (15-45) 3. exhaustive (1-10 hours).  \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI know several others have built benchmarking suites for their internal use, what has been your strategy? \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThoughts, ideas, insights?\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThanks,\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nGrant\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"gsingers\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12440990_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=gsingers\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"gsingers\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Grant Ingersoll\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12440990_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'09\\/Oct\\/06 22:09\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2006-10-09T22:09:28+0000\'\u003e09\\/Oct\\/06 22:09\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    OK, I have a preliminary implementation based on adapting Andrzej\'s approach.  The interesting thing about this approach, is it is easy to adapt to be more or less exhaustive (i.e. how many of the parameters does one wish to have the system alter as it runs)  Thus, you can have it change the merge factors, max buffered docs, number of documents indexed, number of different queries run, etc.  The tradeoff, of course, is the length of time it takes to run these. \\n\\n So my question to those interested, is what is a good baseline running time for testing in a standard way?  My initial thought is to have something that takes between 15-30 minutes to run, but I am not sure on this.  Another approach would be to have three \\\"baselines\\\":  1. quick validation (5 minutes to run...) 2. standard (15-45) 3. exhaustive (1-10 hours).   \\n\\n I know several others have built benchmarking suites for their internal use, what has been your strategy?  \\n\\n Thoughts, ideas, insights? \\n\\n Thanks, \\nGrant              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eOK, here is a first crack at a standard benchmark contribution based on Andrzej original contribution and some updates\\/changes by me.  I wasn\'t nearly as ambitious  as some of the comments attached here, but I think most of them are good things to strive for and will greatly benefit Lucene.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI checked in the basic contrib directory structure, plus some library dependencies, as I wasn\'t sure how svn diff handles those.  I am posting this in patch format to solicit comments first instead of just committing and accepting patches.  My thoughts are I\'ll take a round of comments and make updates as warranted and then make an initial commit.  \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI am particularly interested in the interface\\/Driver specification and whether people think this approach is useful or not.  My thoughts behind it were it might be nice to have a standard way of creating\\/running benchmarks that could be driven by XML configuration files (some examples are in the conf directory).  I am not 100% sold on this and am open to compelling arguments why we should just have each benchmark have it\'s own main() method.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eAs for the actual Benchmarker, I have created a \\\"standard\\\" version, which runs off the Reuters collection that is downloaded automatically by the ANT task.  There are two ANT targets for the two benchmarks: run-micro-standard and run-standard.  The micro version takes a few minutes to run on my machine (it indexes 2000 docs), the other one takes a lot longer.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThere are several support classes in the stats and util packages.  The stats package supports building and maintaining information about benchmarks.  The utils package contains one class for extracting information out of the Reuters documents for indexing.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThe ReutersQueries class contains a set of Queries I created by looking at some of the docs in the collection and are a myriad of term, phrase, span, wildcard and other types of queries.  They aren\'t exhaustive by any means.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIt should be stressed that these benchmarks are best used in gathering before and after numbers.  Furthermore, these aren\'t the be all end all of benchmarking for Lucene.  I hope the interface nature will encourage others to submit benchmarks for specific areas of Lucene not covered by this version.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThanks to all who contributed their code\\/thoughts.  Patch to follow\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"gsingers\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12447346_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=gsingers\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"gsingers\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Grant Ingersoll\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12447346_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'06\\/Nov\\/06 03:23\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2006-11-06T03:23:14+0000\'\u003e06\\/Nov\\/06 03:23\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    OK, here is a first crack at a standard benchmark contribution based on Andrzej original contribution and some updates\\/changes by me.  I wasn\'t nearly as ambitious  as some of the comments attached here, but I think most of them are good things to strive for and will greatly benefit Lucene. \\n\\n I checked in the basic contrib directory structure, plus some library dependencies, as I wasn\'t sure how svn diff handles those.  I am posting this in patch format to solicit comments first instead of just committing and accepting patches.  My thoughts are I\'ll take a round of comments and make updates as warranted and then make an initial commit.   \\n\\n I am particularly interested in the interface\\/Driver specification and whether people think this approach is useful or not.  My thoughts behind it were it might be nice to have a standard way of creating\\/running benchmarks that could be driven by XML configuration files (some examples are in the conf directory).  I am not 100% sold on this and am open to compelling arguments why we should just have each benchmark have it\'s own main() method. \\n\\n As for the actual Benchmarker, I have created a \\\"standard\\\" version, which runs off the Reuters collection that is downloaded automatically by the ANT task.  There are two ANT targets for the two benchmarks: run-micro-standard and run-standard.  The micro version takes a few minutes to run on my machine (it indexes 2000 docs), the other one takes a lot longer. \\n\\n There are several support classes in the stats and util packages.  The stats package supports building and maintaining information about benchmarks.  The utils package contains one class for extracting information out of the Reuters documents for indexing. \\n\\n The ReutersQueries class contains a set of Queries I created by looking at some of the docs in the collection and are a myriad of term, phrase, span, wildcard and other types of queries.  They aren\'t exhaustive by any means. \\n\\n It should be stressed that these benchmarks are best used in gathering before and after numbers.  Furthermore, these aren\'t the be all end all of benchmarking for Lucene.  I hope the interface nature will encourage others to submit benchmarks for specific areas of Lucene not covered by this version. \\n\\n Thanks to all who contributed their code\\/thoughts. I initially thought of a setting where we define tasks\\/jobs that are parameterized, like:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cul class=\\\"alternate\\\" type=\\\"square\\\"\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003ecreateIndex(params)\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003ewriteToIndex(params):\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eaddDocs()\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eoptimize()\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003ereadFromIndex(params):\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003esearchIndex()\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003efetchData()\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e..and compose a test by an XML that says which of these simple jobs to run, with what params, in which order, serial\\/parallel, how long\\/often etc. \u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nThen creating a different test is as easy as creating a different XML that configures that test. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eOn the other hand, chances are, I know, that most useful cases would be those already defined here - standard and micro-standard, so can ask \\\"why bothering changing to define these building blocks\\\". I am not sure here, but thought I\'ll bring it up. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eAbout Using the driver - seems nice and clean to me. I don\'t know the Digester but it seems to read the config from the XML correctly.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eOther comments:\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n1. Seems that rec\\/sec would be a bit more accurately computed by aggregating elapsed times (instead of rate) in showRunData()\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n3. If TimeData not found (only memData) I think additional 0.0 should be printed\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n4. columns allignments with tabs and floats is imperfect.\u003cimg class=\\\"emoticon\\\" src=\\\"\\/jira\\/images\\/icons\\/emoticons\\/smile.png\\\" height=\\\"16\\\" width=\\\"16\\\" align=\\\"absmiddle\\\" alt=\\\"\\\" border=\\\"0\\\"\\/\u003e\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n5. I initially thought of a setting where we define tasks\\/jobs that are parameterized, like: \\n\\n \\n\\t createIndex(params) \\n\\t writeToIndex(params): \\n\\t addDocs() \\n\\t optimize() \\n\\t readFromIndex(params): \\n\\t searchIndex() \\n\\t fetchData() \\n \\n\\n\\n ..and compose a test by an XML that says which of these simple jobs to run, with what params, in which order, serial\\/parallel, how long\\/often etc.  \\nThen creating a different test is as easy as creating a different XML that configures that test.  \\n\\n On the other hand, chances are, I know, that most useful cases would be those already defined here - standard and micro-standard, so can ask \\\"why bothering changing to define these building blocks\\\". I am not sure here, but thought I\'ll bring it up.  \\n\\n About Using the driver - seems nice and clean to me. I don\'t know the Digester but it seems to read the config from the XML correctly. \\n\\n Other comments: \\n1. I think there is a redundant call to params.showRunData(params.getId()) in runBenchmark(File,Options); \\n2. Seems that rec\\/sec would be a bit more accurately computed by aggregating elapsed times (instead of rate) in showRunData() \\n3. If TimeData not found (only memData) I think additional 0.0 should be printed \\n4. columns allignments with tabs and floats is imperfect.  \\n5. It would be nice I think to also get a summary of the results by \\\"task\\\" - e.g. srch, optimize, something like: \\n      &#91;java&#93;  # testData id     operation           runCnt     recCnt          rec\\/s       avgFreeMem      avgTotalMem \\n      &#91;java&#93;                    warm                    60       2000       42,628.8        8,235,758       23,048,192 \\n      &#91;java&#93;                    srch                   120          1          571.4        8,300,613       23,048,192 \\n      &#91;java&#93;                    optimize                 1          1            2.9        9,375,732       23,048,192 \\n      &#91;java&#93;                    trav                   120        107       30,517.8        8,326,046       23,048,192 \\n      &#91;java&#93;                    addDocument              1       2000          441.8        7,310,929       22,206,872 \\n\\n Attached timedata.zip has modifies TimeData.java and TestData.java for  &#91;1 to 5&#93;  above, and for the NAN\\/inifinite.               \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n would like to submit this code in a few days - it is running already but some functionality is missing.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI would like to describe how it works to hopefully get early feedback. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThere are several \\\"basic tasks\\\" defined - all extending an (abstract) class PerfTask:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\u003cul class=\\\"alternate\\\" type=\\\"square\\\"\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eAddDocTask\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eOptimizeTask\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eCreateIndexTask\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\netc. \u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eTo further extend the benchmark \'framework\', new tasks can be added. Each task must implement the abstract method: doLogic(). For instance, in AddDocTask this method (doLogic) would call indexWriter.addDocument().\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nThere are also setup() and tearDown() methods for performing work that should not be timed for that task. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eA special TaskSequence task contains other tasks. It is either parallel or sequential, which tells if it executes its child tasks serially or in parallel. \u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nTaskSequence also supports \\\"rate\\\": the pace in which its child tasks are \\\"fired\\\" can be controlled.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eWith these tasks, it is possible to describe a performance test \'algorithm\' in a simple syntax.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n(\'algorithm\' may be too big a word for this...?)\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eA test invocation takes two parameters: \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\u003cul class=\\\"alternate\\\" type=\\\"square\\\"\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003etest.properties - file with various config properties.\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003etest.alg               - file with the algorithm.\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eBy convention, for each task class  \\\"OpNameTask\\\",  the command  \\\"OpName\\\"  is valid in test.alg.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eAdding a single document is done by:\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    AddDoc\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eAdding 3 documents:\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n   AddDoc\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n   AddDoc\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n   AddDoc\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eOr, alternatively:\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n   \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n{ AddDoc }\\n\u003cp\u003e : 3\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eSo, \'\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n{\' and \'}\\n\u003cp\u003e\' indicate a serial sequence of (child) tasks. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eTo fire 100 queries in a row:\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n  \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n{ Search } : 100\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nTo fire 100 queries in parallel:\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n  [ Search ] : 100\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nSo, \'\u003cspan class=\\\"error\\\"\u003e&#91;&#39; and &#39;&#93;\u003c\\/span\u003e\' indicate a parallel group of tasks. \u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nTo fire 100 queries in a row, 2 queries per second (120 per minute):\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n  { Search }\\n\u003cp\u003e : 100 : 120\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eSimilar, but in parallel:\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n  [ Search ] : 100 : 120\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eA sequence task can be named for identifying it in reports:\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n  \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n{ \\\"QueriesA\\\" Search }\\n\u003cp\u003e : 100 : 120\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eAnd there are tasks that create reports. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThere are more tasks, and more to tell on the alg syntax, but this post is already long..\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI find this quite powerful for perf testing.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nWhat do you (and you) think?\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cul class=\\\"alternate\\\" type=\\\"square\\\"\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eDoron\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"doronc\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Doron Cohen\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12449117_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'12\\/Nov\\/06 10:01\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2006-11-12T10:01:34+0000\'\u003e12\\/Nov\\/06 10:01\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    I looked at extending the benchmark with: \\n \\n\\t different test \\\"scenarios\\\", i.e. other sequences of operations. \\n\\t multithreaded tests, e.g. several queries in parallel. \\n\\t rate of events, e.g. \\\"2 queries arriving per second\\\", or \\\"one query per second in parallel with 20 new documents in a minute\\\". \\n\\t different data sources (input documents, queries). \\n \\n\\n\\n For this I made lots of changes to the benchmark code, using parts of it and rewriting other parts.  \\nI would like to submit this code in a few days - it is running already but some functionality is missing. \\n\\n I would like to describe how it works to hopefully get early feedback.  \\n\\n There are several \\\"basic tasks\\\" defined - all extending an (abstract) class PerfTask: \\n \\n\\t AddDocTask \\n\\t OptimizeTask \\n\\t CreateIndexTask \\netc.  \\n \\n\\n\\n To further extend the benchmark \'framework\', new tasks can be added. Each task must implement the abstract method: doLogic(). For instance, in AddDocTask this method (doLogic) would call indexWriter.addDocument(). \\nThere are also setup() and tearDown() methods for performing work that should not be timed for that task.  \\n\\n A special TaskSequence task contains other tasks. It is either parallel or sequential, which tells if it executes its child tasks serially or in parallel.  \\nTaskSequence also supports \\\"rate\\\": the pace in which its child tasks are \\\"fired\\\" can be controlled. \\n\\n With these tasks, it is possible to describe a performance test \'algorithm\' in a simple syntax. \\n(\'algorithm\' may be too big a word for this...?) \\n\\n A test invocation takes two parameters:  \\n \\n\\t test.properties - file with various config properties. \\n\\t test.alg               - file with the algorithm. \\n \\n\\n\\n By convention, for each task class  \\\"OpNameTask\\\",  the command  \\\"OpName\\\"  is valid in test.alg. \\n\\n Adding a single document is done by: \\n    AddDoc \\n\\n Adding 3 documents: \\n   AddDoc \\n   AddDoc \\n   AddDoc \\n\\n Or, alternatively: \\n    \\n{ AddDoc }\\n  : 3 \\n\\n So, \' \\n{\' and \'}\\n \' indicate a serial sequence of (child) tasks.  \\n\\n To fire 100 queries in a row: \\n   \\n{ Search } : 100 \\n \\nTo fire 100 queries in parallel: \\n  [ Search ] : 100 \\n \\nSo, \' &#91;&#39; and &#39;&#93; \' indicate a parallel group of tasks.  \\n \\nTo fire 100 queries in a row, 2 queries per second (120 per minute): \\n  { Search }\\n  : 100 : 120 \\n\\n Similar, but in parallel: \\n  [ Search ] : 100 : 120 \\n\\n A sequence task can be named for identifying it in reports: \\n   \\n{ \\\"QueriesA\\\" Search }\\n  : 100 : 120 \\n\\n And there are tasks that create reports.  \\n\\n There are more tasks, and more to tell on the alg syntax, but this post is already long.. \\n\\n I find this quite powerful for perf testing. \\nWhat do you (and you) think? \\n\\n \\n\\t Doron \\n \\n             \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv id=\\\"comment-12449118\\\" class=\\\"issue-data-block activity-comment twixi-block  expanded\\\"\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap verbose actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Collapse comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-expanded\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eHide\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-links\\\"\u003e\\n                \u003ca Before submitting the patch file, I tried to apply it myself on a clean version of the code, just to make sure that it works. But I got errors like this &#8211; Could not retrieve revision 0 of \\\"...\\\\byTask\\\\..\\\" &#8211; for every file under a new folder. So I am not sure if it is just my (Windows) svn patch applying utility, or is it really impossible to apply a patch that creates files in (yet) nonexistent directories.  I searched Lucene mailing lists and SVN mailing lists and went again through the SVN book again but nowhere could I find what is the expected behavior for applying a patch containing new directories. In fact, \\\"svn diff\\\" would not even show you files that are new (again, this is the Windows svn 1.4.2 version). (I used Tortoise SVN to create the patch). So I am not sure if it is just my (Windows) svn patch applying utility, or is it really impossible to apply a patch that creates files in (yet) nonexistent directories.  I searched Lucene mailing lists and SVN mailing lists and went again through the SVN book again but nowhere could I find what is the expected behavior for applying a patch containing new directories. In fact, \\\"svn diff\\\" would not even show you files that are new (again, this is the Windows svn 1.4.2 version). (I used Tortoise SVN to create the patch). This is rather annoying and I might be misunderstanding something basic about SVN, but I thought it\'d be better to share this experience here - might save some time for others trying to apply this patch or other patches...              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv
